All Reviews

  1. I bought this at Walmart for $99 in April 2015. I love the travel case, easy to clean and holds the parts tight (and I lugged it around a suitcase from hotel to hotel for about 4 days. It did take a full 24 hrs (about) to charge, which I did before I even turned it on. The brush head spins super fast and even though it alerts you every 30 secs it will keep on after the 2 minute mark. I usually brush my teeth a bit longer. I've used the Oral-B 3D White rechargable toothbrush prior and it did good, but I didn't know what I was missing till I turned this baby on the first time. It's been a week and I still haven't had to charge it. I usually brush 2x daily. I'll update when I do finally charge it.
  2. seemed to work well for the first 1.5 years...after that it hasn't worked correctly (won't sync with the timer, timer jumps around during middle of a brushing).<br /><br />I did seem to have great results when visiting the dentist.
  3. Win number one is using a good quality powered toothbrush like this one versus a non-powered brush. It is far superior to a regular high quality toothbrush.<br /><br />Win number two is the Oral-B brush itself. It feels good using it and it does a good job as a powered toothbrush.<br /><br />Win number three is the BT and android app integration. This is the big win.<br /><br />Briefly, wins one and two are a no brainer. These brushes are on the market and have stayed in the market at many price points because they work, people like them and feel they get good results with them. I've personally been using a powered brush since sometime in 2004 I think. Back then I bought one of the [[ASIN:B007ZN5ATQ Sonicare]] brushes. I used that until it finally actually broke apart sometime in 2009. In 2009 I got another [[ASIN:B0019ZEVZU Sonicare ]], the Healthy White model, and I still have it only putting it aside to test this Oral-B brush for Vine. I am very happy with my Sonicare and probably wouldn't have even bothered with this Oral-B but for the bluetooth integration. I love geeky stuff and what's geekier than a toothbrush with bluetooth?? lol<br /><br />Which brings us to win number three. Bluetooth integration. It is hard to imagine an idea that lends itself to silly overkill criticism like putting BT into a toothbrush handle. But! It is genius! A truism about change is that to effect change you must be able to measure what you want to change. The more measurable something is the more amenable to change it becomes. If you want to brush your teeth more often or more effectively you have to figure out some way of measuring what you are doing now to make positive changes. Oral-B's app and BT enabled handle takes that principle to an awesome place.<br /><br />These powered brushes, the two I've owned, have vibrate timers built-in to prod you to move to the next zone of teeth. That's fine. This app and BT communication synchronize with the app's timer so you can count up or down to the recommended two minute mark. That's cool and neat but not anything more than an 99 cent egg timer could do for you with a non-powered brush. What this device and that app give you is customizable timers, tracking progress over time, a history of activity (condensed), reminders (I didn't bother with this), gentle condemnation, rewards and the current brushing mode. Wow.<br /><br />I added 20 seconds of focused care to my front teeth. That begins as soon as the default 2 minute timer is up. I also spend a little unscheduled time in whitening mode after the focused care - made very, very easy by pushing the select button and seeing the mode change on the app till I get to whitening mode. After the session the app congratulates you on mission accomplished or gives you a frowny if you didn't go the whole way heh. It tracks total and session average time by the day, week and month as well as how many times you brushed your teeth per day.<br /><br />The cool thing about all of that is that you become your own source of peer pressure to brush your teeth. Tired? Too tired to brush? Yeah, but if you skip it the app will know and your average time will drop.<br /><br />Do you play modern video games? You know how lots of games have trophies of some sort? Just little accomplishments you can achieve? This app has them too. So you get a trophy for all sorts of silly stuff that reinforces good brushing habits.<br /><br />Maybe none of that applies to you because you are a nut about brushing your teeth. If that is the case you may be the person that enjoys this product more than anyone else. There's nothing like being recognized for your hard work but who's going to know that you spent a little extra time on your teeth or haven't missed a day in six months? Nobody. Nobody, that is, until now - now you get an app that recognizes and rewards your diligence.<br /><br />Sold? I hope so. I love this toothbrush (and toothbrushes like it) and I think you will too.<br /><br />Some miscellaneous stuff.<br /><br />I don't care what the mfg says. Do not store the handle on the plugged-in charger. My first Sonicare lasted about five years before physically falling apart. My second one has lasted five years and is still going. I read through some of those reviews before writing this review and there were plenty that mentioned the handle just stopped working. Don't constantly charge your handle by storing it on the plugged-in charging base. The charge lasts a long time so there is no need to do that. With the Sonicare handles I'd just use them until they completely discharged. With this handle, because of the tracking app, I use it for six days and set it on the charging base the same day every week. I recommend you do that too.<br /><br />I love the travel case this brush comes with. The handle has a push in spot and the head has a push in spot. Since I don't store the handle on the charging base the travel case is very handy and I use it every day. Great value added item.<br /><br />The brush head is round with this model versus the Sonicare's more traditional rectangle shaped head. I have come to really enjoy this smaller per tooth focusable shape and size with the Oral-B.<br /><br />The Oral-B app is a huge 32mb in size. I find the tendency for apps to be huge very annoying. Phone technology improves so often I do not want to buy an expensive one with a lot of internal storage just to replace it in 12 months. Apps like this make it a hassle to manage which fat bloated app to keep or uninstall. Oral-B should work to improve that.<br /><br />If the idea of using your phone and the app to brush your teeth better is a non-starter for you then, please, still purchase a powered handle just get a quality one without the BT. It is worth it.<br /><br />About eight years ago, a couple of years after getting my first powered brush, my then-GF told me she couldn't understand how I kept my teeth so much whiter than hers lol. I smoke and drink coffee - she doesn't. That was the best testimony I ever heard about the benefits of owning and using a good quality handle like this one. Don't get me wrong, I don't have movie star pearly white teeth and I don't think one of these brushes alone with do that for you but it will do everything better than a $2 non-powered brush will do times infinity.<br /><br />Quality powered toothbrushes are well worth the investment.ome miscellaneous stuff.<br /><br />I don't care what the mfg says.   8. Ever since I started using the Oral-B Pro 4000s and above, my dental hygenist has loved me (well, she likes me and loves how clean my teeth are). They do a fabulous job cleaning, keeping tartar levels low and keeping gums healthy. I only use the standard brushing mode on these models (the 5000 comes with five modes). I brush each quadrant for 30 seconds (the built in timer on the toothbrush tells you when your 30 seconds are up by doing a funny rotation of the toothbrush head). Two minutes later, voila, my teeth are clean.<br /><br />The 4000 model simply has a built in timer and multiple modes. The last 5000 I had provided an external screen which kept track of your brushing progress. I found that screen completely unnecessary, although kids might like it (which might motivate them to brush better). On this 5000, that screen has been replaced by a Bluetooth connection and a phone app to allow your phone to do the thing the external screen once did. Sad to say, I can't test the app out because it requires Bluetooth 4.0 and my phone, an iPhone 4, only has Bluetooth 2.0. It wouldn't matter. I wouldn't use it anyway.<br /><br />This model comes with a different head than the traditional small circular Oral-B head and also different than the newer oval shaped head with a vibrating tip. I've found the oval shaped head to be too hard on my gums. The one provided with this model, a large circular shaped head, seems to be a compromise between the two I've used before. I like it, although I have a stock of small circular brushes in my drawer and will continue to use them when this new one wears out.<br /><br />The one odd thing to note with this newest model is that it flashes ridiculously bright when it's charging. If you keep your brush on your recharging stand all the time when it's not in use, you probably won't notice this. But I only charge when the unit shows a red light. When I put this model on the charging stand, the blue flashing light filled the bathroom, so much so that it was disturbing me in my bedroom. I've since moved my once a week charging to the laundry room.<br /><br />For someone like me, the 4000 model or 3000 models, which have the same fast brushing speeds, would be good enough. If you want the deep cleaning mode and Bluetooth, spend the extra money and get a 5000.bathroom, so much so that it was disturbing me in my bedroom. I've since moved my once a week charging to the laundry room.<br /><br />For someone like me, the 4000 model or 3000 models, which have the same fast brushing speeds, would be good enough. I missed the indicator lights on my old power toothbrush, but it only took a few brushings to adapt.<br /><br />My preferred mode is Deep Clean, but if you are new to power brushes you'll want to start at Sensitive, move to Daily Clean and then move to Deep Clean for your daily regime to avoid bleeding gums, etc (as you'll read about in some reviews). The brush comes with Oral-B's advanced brush head, but you can separately order brush heads for sensitive gums, teeth whitening and braces.<br /><br />The second best feature to the cleaning performance of this brush is its professional timer. On Deep Clean mode, I begin brushing in the left top quadrant of my mouth. At the end of 45 seconds the brush makes an audible stutter and flashes a light to let me know to move to the next quadrant. After two more times and a total of 3 minutes, the brush turns off and I'm done.<br /><br />It also has Bluetooth, which isn't as cool of an add on as I'd hoped. If the power brush with Bluetooth and my smartphone could interact and identify potential problem areas before I needed a dentist, THAT would be cool. As it is, it pretty much just works to create a diary of when I brushed. It could be handy if I had memory issues, but really, if I forgot whether I brushed, I'd just go brush again.<br /><br />Also in the box was a functional, utilitarian travel case, a charging cord and stand with a four brush holder. If I had to give an improvement opportunity, I would suggest offering a lower priced identical model, except without the Bluetooth.nal, utilitarian travel case, a charging cord and stand with a four brush holder. If I had to give an improvement opportunity, I would suggest offering a lower priced identical model, except without the Bluetooth.
  13. Braun Oral-B's Pro 5000 SmartSeries electric toothbrush is very sophisticated and cleans effectively and gently.<br /><br />The Oral-B is very nicely made from a combination of glossy and rubberized white plastic. It feels great in the hand and balances well. It looks very futuristic and modern. Included with the Braun is a charging base/toothbrush caddy and a brittle plastic travel case (speaking of traveling, the battery lasts up to 10 days on a charge). Additionally, you'll get one round toothbrush head.<br /><br />For a toothbrush, the Oral-B is loaded with features. It has 5 brushing modes (regular, extended, sensitive, whitening, and massaging). It also has a built-in interval timer to let you know when 30 seconds have passed so you can move to the next quadrant of your mouth. Lastly, it has a bright red indicator light to let you know when you are pushing too hard.<br /><br />The highlight feature of this Oral-B is its built-in Bluetooth. By downloading a free app, it will connect with your Smartphone so you can keep track of your brushing progress. Oral-B has had a feature like this before, in the form of a separate little display, but having it built into a Smartphone is new, and convenient. I downloaded the app to my iPhone 5s and it hooked up with the toothbrush instantly, and worked flawlessly. While you're brushing your teeth you can check out the news stories that appear at the bottom of the app or switch over to your browser, and it will remember your progress. The app will also keep track of your brushing consistency, encouraging you to brush for a full 2 minutes twice daily. You can even use the app to disable some of the brushing modes that you don't use.<br /><br />Cleaning performance of the Oral-B is high and leaves my teeth squeaky clean and my breath fresh. I like to use the normal mode followed by 30 seconds of whitening in the morning, and extended cleaning and 30 seconds of gum massaging at night. I've never had any issues with bleeding or sensitivity using the Oral-B either. I, however, have been using some sort of electric toothbrush for years. If this is your first electric toothbrush, you may want to start out brushing in the sensitive mode until your mouth adjusts.<br /><br />All in all... a great electric toothbrush, with a handy app.<br /><br />02/26/2015 Update: When I stream audio from my iPhone to a Bluetooth speaker, while I'm using the Oral-B app, the app freaks out and keeps resetting.   14. It's good to see that Oral-B has upgraded the 5000 SmartSeries power toothbrush with a decent smartphone app and ditched the previously included, cumbersome Smartguide device (a small wifi device with limited functionality that displayed the time and a countdown clock of your brushing cycle).<br /><br />If you're familiar with the PRO 5000/7000 series of toothbrushes there's not much that has changed with the brush itself. The battery charge indicator has been updated with a new led-light display pattern but everything else is familiar and same. You're getting the 5 brush modes, a vibration and light-flash pattern every 25% into the cycle and the immensely satisfying finish that the '3D Action' brush head oscillation and pulsation provides.<br /><br />The most interesting update to the 5000 series is the utilization of Bluetooth technology that allows your brush to sync up with your smartphone to monitor current brushing progress, measure the last 6 months of your brushing history and intuitively make a series of adjustments to the device itself that truly personalizes your individual brushing experience. While brushing the app will keep you informed and entertained with featured content such as top news stories, local weather or a slideshow of pics from your personal albums amongst many other options. Sounds frivolous, yes? I initially thought so but it sure beats staring at yourself in the mirror for 2+ minutes and truly makes the brushing session go by in a jiff.<br /><br />There's also the addition of gamification features via the inclusion of 40 trophies (eg - '7 Day Brushing Streak') that demonstrates a promising embrace of networked user engagement practices in the otherwise mundane and forgettable task of your daily tooth hygiene. I imagine that these initial batch of trophies are just the beginning and future updates will add new engagement loops (eg - unlock 'x' trophy and get a free brush head) and perhaps offer demographic-specific activities such as an adventure game for kids that only allows progress as they brush each day.<br /><br />Stat junkies in search of another data source to feed into their quantified lifestyle will also appreciate the 6 months of brushing history the app stores that pinpoints a variety of data sets including moments when you were brushing too hard, your flossing/mouthwash/tongue cleaning patterns amongst many others.<br /><br />Overall, Oral-B's inclusion of smart networking on their new brushes is a very promising start (the features currently offered through the synced app is just the beginning) and I look forward to experiencing the expansion and evolution of this particular service. One day, in a not so distant future, these brushes will have SIRI like conversations with us and when that happens - I for one, welcome our new power toothbrush Overlords.adventure game for kids that only allows progress as they brush each day.<br /><br />Stat junkies in search of another data source to feed into their quantified lifestyle will also appreciate the 6 months of brushing history the app stores that pinpoints a variety of data sets including moments when you were brushing too hard, your flossing/mouthwash/tongue cleaning patterns amongst many others.<br /><br />Overall, Oral-B's inclusion of smart networking on their new brushes is a very promising start (the features currently offered through the synced app is just the beginning) and I look forward to experiencing the expansion and evolution of this particular service.   108. Given that I'm a little of a data nerd, the reason I bought the Pro 5000 is so that I would force myself to do a better job brushing my teeth and gums. Given this, I have to review both the toothbrush and the related application.<br /><br />Toothbrush – 4 stars<br />The toothbrush works exceptionally well. I love that the LED turns red when I’m pressing too hard against my teeth and gums. I love that it pulses when it’s time to change quadrant and pulses more strongly when I’ve reached my target time.<br />To get the 5th star, the toothbrush needs to address the following:<br />1. When I change to total brush time from 2 to 3 minutes, I expect that the toothbrush adjusts the time to brush per quadrant. When set to 2 minutes, each quadrant takes 30 seconds (4 x 30 sec = 120 sec). When set to 3 minutes (what Oral-b calls Deep Clean or 2 minutes + 1), the toothbrush wants me to change at the following rate: (Quad-1) after 30 seconds, (Quad-2) after 45 seconds, (Quad-3) after 45 seconds, (Quad-4) after 45 seconds. This means that Quad-1 was only brushed for 30 seconds and there still is 15 seconds to go in the 3 minutes. Also, there is no indication when you reach the 3-minute mark. Instead, I expected that I would be reminded to change quadrant after 45 seconds and that end-of-job indicator would vibrate at the 3-minute mark.<br />2. When set to Deep Clean (3 minutes of brushing), disable the 2-minute end-of-brushing mark and set it at 3 minutes instead.<br />3. Recharging a discharged toothbrush takes a long time, close to 48 hours for me. I expect it to recharge overnight (8-10 hours).<br />Note: For what it’s worth, my firmware version is: SW-Version 05, P-Version: 01<br /><br />Oral-B App – 2 stars<br />I’m using Android version of the Oral-B app (version 2.1.2). I love how it prompts you to go from quadrant to quadrant. The graphics and user interface are excellent. I also enjoy the little motivation tricks it displays. Finally, I like how I can customize its settings. For example, I only want to be prompted to brush my tongue in the morning and use a fluoride rinse in the evening but remind me to floss every time. The application then tracks all of these, providing of course you use them honestly. However, I found the following very annoying defects for a product this expensive:<br />1. I have not yet been able to pairing the toothbrush with my Samsung S5 and the application. I’m putting this here instead of in the toothbrush section, because this doesn’t really impact the use of the brush. I’m prompted for a PIN and none was given in the documentation. So I tried the usual ones without success.<br />2. After using the toothbrush for close to 3 months, I have never been able to synchronize my off-line brushing sessions with the application even though I’m trying different ways to pair the app with the brush. Even though the app and the brush as not formally paired, the application seems to be able to communicate with the brush. It senses when I briefly interrupt my brushing and resumes where I left off, I senses when I’m done brushing and when I press too hard on my gums (the screen on the smartphone turns red), etc.<br />3. The time indicator on the app is always set to 2:00 even when both the app and the toothbrush know that I will be doing what Oral-B calls a Deep Clean (3 minutes of brushing). I expect the setting to be 3:00 in this case.<br />4. The app hiccups when I start brushing my teeth before it had a chance to try to retrieve prior brushing sessions. In other words, the clock will start with my brushing session for say 10 seconds, then it will reset to 2:00. Sometimes stopping the brush for a few seconds then restarting will correct this.<br />5. I’ve had the app stop recording in the middle of sessions and give me the very disappointed face that I didn’t brush for at least 2 minutes when in fact I was still brushing.<br />6. The Oral-b website is abysmal whentrying to find support for the points above. There are no forums or an effective Q&A section to answer user questions. That’s very strange in this era of crowd-sourcing help and answers. Ironically, the best site I’ve found for answers is the Amazon Review section.<br /><br />Summary – 3 stars<br />Given the price of the toothbrush, Braun’s reputation for quality, and Braun’s attempt at migrating consumers away from Philips’ Sonicare brand, I expected more from this purchase. Bluetooth is meant to bind together a pretty good toothbrush with a smartphone application to make a superior user experience. That goal is far from being reached. The toothbrush, on its own, is very effective and motivates me to at least brush for 2 minutes per session and lets me know when I’m pressing too hard against my gums. Only you can decide whether this is worth the price of the toothbrush. I like mine.he points above. There are no forums or an effective Q&A section to answer user questions. It's really a bit of a pain to remember to bring my phone to the bathroom, unlock the phone, start the app, then start brushing every time. While you're brushing the app pretty much gives you the same info that you get with the smart guide that Oral B has included with their toothbrushes for a while now (although it does also include news headlines, weather information, and upcoming calendar appointments) but frankly,when I first got my triumph brush I think I used the smart guide for all of about a week and then managed to lose it in the back of a bathroom cabinet, so I'm not sure I really see myself continuing to open up the app every time I brush my teeth.<br /><br />The app will also record how often and how long you brush for and the brush will retain 20 sessions if you don't start the app each time you brush, so if you want a log of your brushing habits, then it would be good for this and you'd only have to sync with your phone about every two weeks or so, but frankly, I'm not entirely certain why I'd want a log of how often I brush my teeth.<br /><br />The other thing worth noting is that it doesn't work well to share the brush with someone else. The brush will sync with more than one phone, so if everyone remembers to open the app every time they brush, then it will work and the data will all be logged correctly for each user. However, if you don't open the app the brush will store the session in it's own memory and will then sync that session with the first phone that it connects to. So if my wife wakes up first and brushes her teeth without connecting her phone, then I connect my phone and start brushing the app will show that I brushed my teeth twice that morning... once from the saved session that my wife did and once from when I actually brushed them.<br /><br />So in the end I'm going to keep the brush as I'm really quite happy with it's performance as an electric toothbrush, and the bluetooth feature doesn't really add any additional cost (I believe it's actually the same price as the non-bluetooth Pro 5000), but I'm not sure I'll actually be using the bluetooth feature several weeks from now.e else. The different modes seem to alter the speed of the rotation, whether the pressure sensor is turned on, and I believe the activation of the timer. I have only used the supplied brush head.<br /><br />The app is interesting. For all intents and purposes I would describe the app as an activity monitor with some fluff built in. When on, the app will record how long you brushed for and store that stat. After each brushing the app asks you three questions as to whether or not you flossed, brushed your tongue, and rinsed. Also, recording your answers to those questions. You have the opportunity to view your brushing stats for the day, wee, or month. During the brushing routine, you can set your screen to see just a straight timer, or 3D teeth mode which highlights a quadrant of your mouth that you should be brushing.<br /><br />The app also contains silly things like Achievement badges which are awarded after repeated uses, based on the activity and the time you do it (for instance if you brush your teeth at least 7 times between 3 AM and 6 AM you get a badge). These badges may add some positive reinforcement, but are largely useless. You can also shop for brush heads from the app, but when I tried to connect the store said it was unavailable. This is also true about the Feedback function. I do like the idea that I can customize the routine to fit suggestions from my dentist.<br /><br />So the app is useful, but I can see improvements that will hopefully be introduced into future models. I purposely tested this twice. I left my Bluetooth off on my phone and did a brushing session. One time it updated my profile with the missing session, the other time it did not. I wish there was a way to manually update the info.   238. I expected to be impressed with the features on this electric toothbrush. Wow, Bluetooth technology! Now, I am thinking, why? The Oral B electric toothbrush works well without any extra technology. It does a thorough job. It gets the teeth that are way in the back, and as a bonus, I do not gag while brushing with this toothbrush. However, the negative aspects of this toothbrush outweigh the positives.<br /><br />When I showed this toothbrush to my husband, he wondered why anyone would want to bring their cell phone into the bathroom where it could get damaged. He thought it was silly to stand there and brush with a smart phone that really does not do much as far as helping you. Now, I must mention that at the time of this review, I had no cell phone so no Bluetooth was used. However, even without the Bluetooth technology, this SmartSeries is not so smart. When you open the box you get the Oral B Pro 5000 SmartSeries Toothbrush handle or unit, a toothbrush head for one person, a ring that is color coded so you can designate which head is yours (provided you purchase more heads), a travel case, a stand which is also where the unit charges, and a cover for the tray where you place the heads. Also included are the directions. The toothbrush is easy to charge and click onto the stand. The heads pop off and on easily enough too. I thought the cover tray was poorly done since you just place it over the toothbrush heads. It does not click in anywhere so if someone knocks something into it, the cover comes off and then your heads are exposed. The travel case is big and I did not think it was a necessity but it is a nice feature if you travel with your electric toothbrush.<br /><br />Now this Oral B toothbrush supposedly has 2 timer modes for you to set the toothbrush so you get the kind of clean you want. One is professional and the other is the 2 minute mode. Either mode will communicate with you through a stuttering sound and feel. They mention a green light but I never saw the green light on while brushing. I find the stuttering experience annoying since it suddenly stops what I am trying to do. A beep would be better and would not prolong my brushing. Now, the toothbrush comes set in the Professional Mode. Every 30 seconds, it stutters and supposedly a green light comes on to let you know you need to move to the next quadrant of your mouth. I never timed it for accuracy but it seems pretty short to me. I do not need a toothbrush to tell me when it is time to move on. A long stuttering sign indicates that your 2 minute time for the Professional Mode is done. I can't tell the difference and I just continue and turn off the brush when I am done. (I brush longer than the allotted time.) With the 2 minute Mode, it gives a short stuttering sound and a green light when you are done with the two minutes. I have never been able to figure out which mode I am in without turning on the brush and brushing my teeth. There is nothing to indicate which mode you are in.<br /><br />If you put too much pressure on your brush, a red pressure sensor light will light up. I tried this by biting down on the head and I did not see any red light. What do you have to do bite the head off?<br /><br />Now apparently the more advanced model comes with this happy face timer and offers different brushing modes. This toothbrush comes with ONLY the ability to change between the timer modes. There are no different brushing modes like I thought there would be. To me, this is just a gussied up version of a regular Oral B Pro electric toothbrush with Bluetooth technology. Why pay for something that you can determine on your own? Apparently the features of the phone give diagrams, charts, and other info that you can show the dentist. As if your dentist would really start studying that. Most ask if you have been brushing and flossing and take your word for it. They examine you to see if you are doing a good job or not. If someone brushes for 2 minutes, it does not mean that it is a quality job. You have to brush well and the right way in order to keep your teeth in good condition.<br /><br />All in all, I would say the actual brushing without the bells and whistles gives you a wonderful, clean mouth better than a regular, manual toothbrush can. However, I do not think you should spend more money for something that claims to have these amazing features and really doesn't.ean that it is a quality job. You have to brush well and the right way in order to keep your teeth in good condition.<br /><br />All in all, I would say the actual brushing without the bells and whistles gives you a wonderful, clean mouth better than a regular, manual toothbrush can. However, I do not think you should spend more money for something that claims to have these amazing features and really doesn't.
